out of bondag tom liber your truli explanatori in this book a number of dialect are use to wit  the missouri negro dialect the extremest form of the backwood southwestern dialect the ordinari pike counti dialect and four modifi varieti of this last the shade have not been done in a haphazard fashion or by guesswork but painstak and with the trustworthi guidanc and support of person familiar with these sever form of speech i make this explan for the reason that without it mani reader would suppos that all these charact were tri to talk alik and not succeed the author huckleberri finn scene  the mississippi valley time  forti to fifti year ago chapter i you dont know about me without you have read a book by the name of the adventur of tom sawyer but that aint no matter  that book was made by mr mark twain and he told the truth main  there was thing which he stretch but main he told the truth  that is noth  i never seen anybodi but lie one time or anoth without it was aunt polli or the widow or mayb mari  aunt pollytom aunt polli she isand mari and the widow dougla is all told about in that book which is most a true book with some stretcher as i said befor now the way that the book wind up is this  tom and me found the money that the robber hid in the cave and it made us rich  we got six thousand dollar apieceal gold  it was an aw sight of money when it was pile up  well judg thatcher he took it and put it out at interest and it fetch us a dollar a day apiec all the year roundmor than a bodi could tell what to do with  the widow dougla she took me for her son and allow she would sivil me but it was rough live in the hous all the time consid how dismal regular and decent the widow was in all her way and so when i couldnt stand it no longer i lit out  i got into my old rag and my sugar hogshead again and was free and satisfi  but tom sawyer he hunt me up and said he was go to start a band of robber and i might join if i would go back to the widow and be respect  so i went back the widow she cri over me and call me a poor lost lamb and she call me a lot of other name too but she never meant no harm by it she put me in them new cloth again and i couldnt do noth but sweat and sweat and feel all cramp up  well then the old thing commenc again  the widow rung a bell for supper and you had to come to time when you got to the tabl you couldnt go right to eat but you had to wait for the widow to tuck down her head and grumbl a littl over the victual though there warnt realli anyth the matter with themthat is noth onli everyth was cook by itself  in a barrel of odd and end it is differ thing get mix up and the juic kind of swap around and the thing go better after supper she got out her book and learn me about mose and the bulrush and i was in a sweat to find out all about him but by and by she let it out that mose had been dead a consider long time so then i didnt care no more about him becaus i dont take no stock in dead peopl pretti soon i want to smoke and ask the widow to let me  but she wouldnt  she said it was a mean practic and wasnt clean and i must tri to not do it ani more  that is just the way with some peopl  they get down on a thing when they dont know noth about it  here she was a bother about mose which was no kin to her and no use to anybodi be gone you see yet find a power of fault with me for do a thing that had some good in it  and she took snuff too of cours that was all right becaus she done it herself her sister miss watson a toler slim old maid with goggl on had just come to live with her and took a set at me now with a spell book she work me middl hard for about an hour and then the widow made her eas up  i couldnt stood it much longer  then for an hour it was dead dull and i was fidgeti  miss watson would say dont put your feet up there huckleberri and dont scrunch up like that huckleberryset up straight and pretti soon she would say dont gap and stretch like that huckleberrywhi dont you tri to behav  then she told me all about the bad place and i said i wish i was there she got mad then but i didnt mean no harm  all i want was to go somewher all i want was a chang i warnt particular  she said it was wick to say what i said said she wouldnt say it for the whole world she was go to live so as to go to the good place  well i couldnt see no advantag in go where she was go so i made up my mind i wouldnt tri for it  but i never said so becaus it would onli make troubl and wouldnt do no good now she had got a start and she went on and told me all about the good place  she said all a bodi would have to do there was to go around all day long with a harp and sing forev and ever  so i didnt think much of it but i never said so  i ask her if she reckon tom sawyer would go there and she said not by a consider sight  i was glad about that becaus i want him and me to be togeth miss watson she kept peck at me and it got tiresom and lonesom  bi and by they fetch the nigger in and had prayer and then everybodi was off to bed  i went up to my room with a piec of candl and put it on the tabl  then i set down in a chair by the window and tri to think of someth cheer but it warnt no use  i felt so lonesom i most wish i was dead  the star were shine and the leav rustl in the wood ever so mourn and i heard an owl away off who whoo about somebodi that was dead and a whippowil and a dog cri about somebodi that was go to die and the wind was tri to whisper someth to me and i couldnt make out what it was and so it made the cold shiver run over me then away out in the wood i heard that kind of a sound that a ghost make when it want to tell about someth that on it mind and cant make itself understood and so cant rest easi in it grave and has to go about that way everi night griev  i got so down heart and scare i did wish i had some compani  pretti soon a spider went crawl up my shoulder and i flip it off and it lit in the candl and befor i could budg it was all shrivel up  i didnt need anybodi to tell me that that was an aw bad sign and would fetch me some bad luck so i was scare and most shook the cloth off of me i got up and turn around in my track three time and cross my breast everi time and then i tie up a littl lock of my hair with a thread to keep witch away  but i hadnt no confid  you do that when youv lost a horsesho that youv found instead of nail it up over the door but i hadnt ever heard anybodi say it was ani way to keep off bad luck when youd kill a spider i set down again a shake all over and got out my pipe for a smoke for the hous was all as still as death now and so the widow wouldnt know well after a long time i heard the clock away off in the town go boomboomboomtwelv lick and all still againstil than ever pretti soon i heard a twig snap down in the dark amongst the treessometh was a stir  i set still and listen  direct i could just bare hear a me yow me yow down there  that was good  say i me yow me yow as soft as i could and then i put out the light and scrambl out of the window on to the shed  then i slip down to the ground and crawl in among the tree and sure enough there was tom sawyer wait for me chapter ii we went tipto along a path amongst the tree back toward the end of the widow garden stoop down so as the branch wouldnt scrape our head when we was pass by the kitchen i fell over a root and made a nois  we scrouch down and laid still  miss watson big nigger name jim was set in the kitchen door we could see him pretti clear becaus there was a light behind him  he got up and stretch his neck out about a minut listen  then he say who dah he listen some more then he come tipto down and stood right between us we could a touch him near  well like it was minut and minut that there warnt a sound and we all there so close togeth  there was a place on my ankl that got to itch but i dasnt scratch it and then my ear begun to itch and next my back right between my shoulder  seem like id die if i couldnt scratch  well ive notic that thing plenti time sinc  if you are with the qualiti or at a funer or tri to go to sleep when you aint sleepyif you are anywher where it wont do for you to scratch whi you will itch all over in upward of a thousand place pretti soon jim say say who is you  whar is you  dog my cat ef i didn hear sumfn well i know what is gwyne to do  is gwyne to set down here and listen tell i hear it agin so he set down on the ground betwixt me and tom  he lean his back up against a tree and stretch his leg out till one of them most touch one of mine  mi nose begun to itch  it itch till the tear come into my eye  but i dasnt scratch  then it begun to itch on the insid next i got to itch underneath  i didnt know how i was go to set still this miser went on as much as six or seven minut but it seem a sight longer than that  i was itch in eleven differ place now  i reckon i couldnt stand it moren a minut longer but i set my teeth hard and got readi to tri  just then jim begun to breath heavi next he begun to snoreand then i was pretti soon comfort again tom he made a sign to mekind of a littl nois with his mouthand we went creep away on our hand and knee  when we was ten foot off tom whisper to me and want to tie jim to the tree for fun  but i said no he might wake and make a disturb and then theyd find out i warnt in then tom said he hadnt got candl enough and he would slip in the kitchen and get some more  i didnt want him to tri  i said jim might wake up and come  but tom want to resk it so we slid in there and got three candl and tom laid five cent on the tabl for pay then we got out and i was in a sweat to get away but noth would do tom but he must crawl to where jim was on his hand and knee and play someth on him  i wait and it seem a good while everyth was so still and lonesom as soon as tom was back we cut along the path around the garden fenc and by and by fetch up on the steep top of the hill the other side of the hous  tom said he slip jim hat off of his head and hung it on a limb right over him and jim stir a littl but he didnt wake afterward jim said the witch be witch him and put him in a tranc and rode him all over the state and then set him under the tree again and hung his hat on a limb to show who done it  and next time jim told it he said they rode him down to new orlean and after that everi time he told it he spread it more and more till by and by he said they rode him all over the world and tire him most to death and his back was all over saddl boil  jim was monstrous proud about it and he got so he wouldnt hard notic the other nigger  nigger would come mile to hear jim tell about it and he was more look up to than ani nigger in that countri  strang nigger would stand with their mouth open and look him all over same as if he was a wonder  nigger is alway talk about witch in the dark by the kitchen fire but whenev one was talk and let on to know all about such thing jim would happen in and say hm  what you know bout witch and that nigger was cork up and had to take a back seat  jim alway kept that five center piec round his neck with a string and said it was a charm the devil give to him with his own hand and told him he could cure anybodi with it and fetch witch whenev he want to just by say someth to it but he never told what it was he said to it  nigger would come from all around there and give jim anyth they had just for a sight of that five center piec but they wouldnt touch it becaus the devil had had his hand on it  jim was most ruin for a servant becaus he got stuck up on account of have seen the devil and been rode by witch well when tom and me got to the edg of the hilltop we look away down into the villag and could see three or four light twinkl where there was sick folk mayb and the star over us was sparkl ever so fine and down by the villag was the river a whole mile broad and aw still and grand  we went down the hill and found jo harper and ben roger and two or three more of the boy hid in the old tanyard  so we unhitch a skiff and pull down the river two mile and a half to the big scar on the hillsid and went ashor we went to a clump of bush and tom made everybodi swear to keep the secret and then show them a hole in the hill right in the thickest part of the bush  then we lit the candl and crawl in on our hand and knee  we went about two hundr yard and then the cave open up tom poke about amongst the passag and pretti soon duck under a wall where you wouldnt a notic that there was a hole  we went along a narrow place and got into a kind of room all damp and sweati and cold and there we stop  tom say now well start this band of robber and call it tom sawyer gang everybodi that want to join has got to take an oath and write his name in blood everybodi was will  so tom got out a sheet of paper that he had wrote the oath on and read it  it swore everi boy to stick to the band and never tell ani of the secret and if anybodi done anyth to ani boy in the band whichev boy was order to kill that person and his famili must do it and he mustnt eat and he mustnt sleep till he had kill them and hack a cross in their breast which was the sign of the band and nobodi that didnt belong to the band could use that mark and if he did he must be su and if he done it again he must be kill  and if anybodi that belong to the band told the secret he must have his throat cut and then have his carcass burnt up and the ash scatter all around and his name blot off of the list with blood and never mention again by the gang but have a curs put on it and be forgot forev everybodi said it was a real beauti oath and ask tom if he got it out of his own head  he said some of it but the rest was out of pirat book and robber book and everi gang that was high tone had it some thought it would be good to kill the famili of boy that told the secret  tom said it was a good idea so he took a pencil and wrote it in then ben roger say here huck finn he haint got no famili what you go to do bout him well haint he got a father say tom sawyer yes hes got a father but you cant never find him these day  he use to lay drunk with the hog in the tanyard but he haint been seen in these part for a year or more they talk it over and they was go to rule me out becaus they said everi boy must have a famili or somebodi to kill or els it wouldnt be fair and squar for the other  well nobodi could think of anyth to doeverybodi was stump and set still  i was most readi to cri but all at onc i thought of a way and so i offer them miss watsonthey could kill her  everybodi said oh shell do  that all right  huck can come in then they all stuck a pin in their finger to get blood to sign with and i made my mark on the paper now say ben roger what the line of busi of this gang noth onli robberi and murder tom said but who are we go to robhous or cattl or stuff steal cattl and such thing aint robberi it burglari say tom sawyer  we aint burglar  that aint no sort of style  we are highwaymen  we stop stage and carriag on the road with mask on and kill the peopl and take their watch and money must we alway kill the peopl oh certain  it best  some author think differ but most it consid best to kill themexcept some that you bring to the cave here and keep them till theyr ransom ransom  what that i dont know  but that what they do  ive seen it in book and so of cours that what weve got to do but how can we do it if we dont know what it is whi blame it all weve got to do it  dont i tell you it in the book  do you want to go to do differ from what in the book and get thing all muddl up oh that all veri fine to say tom sawyer but how in the nation are these fellow go to be ransom if we dont know how to do it to themthat the thing i want to get at  now what do you reckon it is well i dont know  but perap if we keep them till theyr ransom it mean that we keep them till theyr dead now that someth like  thatll answer  whi couldnt you said that befor  well keep them till theyr ransom to death and a bothersom lot theyll be tooeat up everyth and alway tri to get loos how you talk ben roger  how can they get loos when there a guard over them readi to shoot them down if they move a peg a guard  well that is good  so somebodi got to set up all night and never get ani sleep just so as to watch them  i think that foolish whi cant a bodi take a club and ransom them as soon as they get here becaus it aint in the book sothat whi  now ben roger do you want to do thing regular or dont youthat the idea  dont you reckon that the peopl that made the book know what the correct thing to do  do you reckon you can learn em anyth  not by a good deal no sir well just go on and ransom them in the regular way all right  i dont mind but i say it a fool way anyhow  say do we kill the women too well ben roger if i was as ignor as you i wouldnt let on  kill the women  no nobodi ever saw anyth in the book like that  you fetch them to the cave and your alway as polit as pie to them and by and by they fall in love with you and never want to go home ani more well if that the way im agre but i dont take no stock in it mighti soon well have the cave so clutter up with women and fellow wait to be ransom that there wont be no place for the robber but go ahead i aint got noth to say littl tommi barn was asleep now and when they wake him up he was scare and cri and said he want to go home to his ma and didnt want to be a robber ani more so they all made fun of him and call him cri babi and that made him mad and he said he would go straight and tell all the secret  but tom give him five cent to keep quiet and said we would all go home and meet next week and rob somebodi and kill some peopl ben roger said he couldnt get out much onli sunday and so he want to begin next sunday but all the boy said it would be wick to do it on sunday and that settl the thing  they agre to get togeth and fix a day as soon as they could and then we elect tom sawyer first captain and jo harper second captain of the gang and so start home i clumb up the shed and crept into my window just befor day was break my new cloth was all greas up and clayey and i was dog tire chapter iii well i got a good go over in the morn from old miss watson on account of my cloth but the widow she didnt scold but onli clean off the greas and clay and look so sorri that i thought i would behav awhil if i could  then miss watson she took me in the closet and pray but noth come of it  she told me to pray everi day and whatev i ask for i would get it  but it warnt so  i tri it onc i got a fish line but no hook  it warnt ani good to me without hook  i tri for the hook three or four time but somehow i couldnt make it work  bi and by one day i ask miss watson to tri for me but she said i was a fool  she never told me whi and i couldnt make it out no way i set down one time back in the wood and had a long think about it  i say to myself if a bodi can get anyth they pray for whi dont deacon winn get back the money he lost on pork  whi cant the widow get back her silver snuffbox that was stole  whi cant miss watson fat up no say i to my self there aint noth in it  i went and told the widow about it and she said the thing a bodi could get by pray for it was spiritu gift  this was too mani for me but she told me what she meanti must help other peopl and do everyth i could for other peopl and look out for them all the time and never think about myself this was includ miss watson as i took it  i went out in the wood and turn it over in my mind a long time but i couldnt see no advantag about itexcept for the other peopl so at last i reckon i wouldnt worri about it ani more but just let it go  sometim the widow would take me one side and talk about provid in a way to make a bodi mouth water but mayb next day miss watson would take hold and knock it all down again  i judg i could see that there was two provid and a poor chap would stand consider show with the widow provid but if miss watson got him there warnt no help for him ani more  i thought it all out and reckon i would belong to the widow if he want me though i couldnt make out how he was a go to be ani better off then than what he was befor see i was so ignor and so kind of low down and orneri pap he hadnt been seen for more than a year and that was comfort for me i didnt want to see him no more  he use to alway whale me when he was sober and could get his hand on me though i use to take to the wood most of the time when he was around  well about this time he was found in the river drownd about twelv mile abov town so peopl said  they judg it was him anyway said this drownd man was just his size and was rag and had uncommon long hair which was all like pap but they couldnt make noth out of the face becaus it had been in the water so long it warnt much like a face at all  they said he was float on his back in the water  they took him and buri him on the bank  but i warnt comfort long becaus i happen to think of someth  i know mighti well that a drownd man dont float on his back but on his face  so i know then that this warnt pap but a woman dress up in a man cloth  so i was uncomfort again  i judg the old man would turn up again by and by though i wish he wouldnt we play robber now and then about a month and then i resign  all the boy did  we hadnt rob nobodi hadnt kill ani peopl but onli just pretend  we use to hop out of the wood and go charg down on hog driver and women in cart take garden stuff to market but we never hive ani of them  tom sawyer call the hog ingot and he call the turnip and stuff juleri and we would go to the cave and powwow over what we had done and how mani peopl we had kill and mark  but i couldnt see no profit in it  one time tom sent a boy to run about town with a blaze stick which he call a slogan which was the sign for the gang to get togeth and then he said he had got secret news by his spi that next day a whole parcel of spanish merchant and rich a rab was go to camp in cave hollow with two hundr eleph and six hundr camel and over a thousand sumter mule all load down with dimond and they didnt have onli a guard of four hundr soldier and so we would lay in ambuscad as he call it and kill the lot and scoop the thing  he said we must slick up our sword and gun and get readi  he never could go after even a turnip cart but he must have the sword and gun all scour up for it though they was onli lath and broomstick and you might scour at them till you rot and then they warnt worth a mouth of ash more than what they was befor  i didnt believ we could lick such a crowd of spaniard and a rab but i want to see the camel and eleph so i was on hand next day saturday in the ambuscad and when we got the word we rush out of the wood and down the hill  but there warnt no spaniard and a rab and there warnt no camel nor no eleph  it warnt anyth but a sunday school picnic and onli a primer class at that  we bust it up and chase the children up the hollow but we never got anyth but some doughnut and jam though ben roger got a rag doll and jo harper got a hymn book and a tract and then the teacher charg in and made us drop everyth and cut  i didnt see no dimond and i told tom sawyer so  he said there was load of them there anyway and he said there was a rab there too and eleph and thing  i said whi couldnt we see them then  he said if i warnt so ignor but had read a book call don quixot i would know without ask  he said it was all done by enchant  he said there was hundr of soldier there and eleph and treasur and so on but we had enemi which he call magician and they had turn the whole thing into an infant sunday school just out of spite  i said all right then the thing for us to do was to go for the magician  tom sawyer said i was a numskul whi said he a magician could call up a lot of geni and they would hash you up like noth befor you could say jack robinson  they are as tall as a tree and as big around as a church well i say spose we got some geni to help us cant we lick the other crowd then how you go to get them i dont know  how do they get them whi they rub an old tin lamp or an iron ring and then the geni come tear in with the thunder and lightn a rip around and the smoke a roll and everyth theyr told to do they up and do it  they dont think noth of pull a shot tower up by the root and belt a sunday school superintend over the head with itor ani other man who make them tear around so whi whoever rub the lamp or the ring  they belong emperor daughter from china for you to marri theyv got to do itand theyv got to do it befor sun up next morn too  and more  theyv got to waltz that palac around over the countri wherev you want it you would drop my busi and come to him for the rub of an old tin lamp how you talk huck finn  whi youd have to come when he rub it whether you want to or not what and i as high as a tree and as big as a church  all right then i would come but i lay id make that man climb the highest tree there was in the countri shuck it aint no use to talk to you huck finn  you dont seem to know anyth somehowperfect cheer me up  so the longer i went to school the easier it got to be  i was get sort of use to the widow way too and they warnt so raspi on me  live in a hous and sleep in a bed pull on me pretti tight said i was come along slow but sure and do veri satisfactori  she said she warnt asham of me one morn i happen to turn over the salt cellar at breakfast  i reach for some of it as quick as i could to throw over my left shoulder and keep off the bad luck but miss watson was in ahead of me and cross me off she say take your hand away huckleberri what a mess you are alway make  the widow put in a good word for me but that warnt go to keep off the bad luck i know that well enough  i start out after breakfast feel worri and shaki and wonder where it was go to fall on me and what it was go to be over the stile where you go through the high board fenc  there was an inch of new snow on the ground and i seen somebodi track  they had come up from the quarri and stood around the stile a while and then went on around the garden fenc  it was funni they hadnt come in after stand around so  i couldnt make it out  it was veri curious somehow  i was go to follow around but i stoop down to look at the track first  i didnt notic anyth at first but next i did  there was a cross in the left boot heel made with big nail to keep off the devil i was up in a second and shin down the hill  i look over my shoulder everi now and then but i didnt see nobodi  i was at judg thatcher as quick as i could get there  he said whi my boy you are all out of breath  did you come for your interest no sir i say paper and read it over and say there you see it say for a consider  that mean i have bought it of you and paid you for it  here a dollar for you  now you sign it so i sign it and left miss watson nigger jim had a hair ball as big as your fist which had been took out of the fourth stomach of an ox and he use to do magic with it  he said there was a spirit insid of it and it know everyth  so i went to him that night and told him pap was here again for i found his track in the snow  what i want to know was what he was go to do and was he go to stay  jim got out his hair ball and said someth over it and then he held it up and drop it on the floor  it fell pretti solid and onli roll about an inch  jim tri it again and then anoth time and it act just the same  jim got down on his knee and put his ear against it and listen  but it warnt no use he said it wouldnt talk he said sometim it wouldnt talk without money  i told him i had an old slick counterfeit quarter that warnt no good becaus the brass show through the silver a littl and it wouldnt pass nohow even if the brass didnt show becaus it was so slick it felt greasi and so that would tell on it everi time  i reckon i wouldnt say noth about the dollar i got from the judg i said it was pretti bad money but mayb the hair ball would take it becaus mayb it wouldnt know the differ  jim smelt it and bit it and rub it and said he would manag so the hair ball would think it was good  he said he would split open a raw irish potato and stick the quarter in between and keep it there all night and next morn you couldnt see no brass and it wouldnt feel greasi no more and so anybodi in town would take it in a minut let alon a hair ball  well i know a potato would do that befor but i had forgot it jim put the quarter under the hair ball and got down and listen again this time he said the hair ball was all right  he said it would tell my whole fortun if i want it to  i say go on  so the hair ball talk to jim and jim told it to me  he say yo ole father doan know yit what hes a gwyne to do  sometim he spec hell go way en den agin he spec hell stay  de bes way is to res easi en let de ole man take his own way  dey two angel hoverin roun bout him  one uv em is white en shini en tother one is black de white one git him to go right a littl while den de black one sail in en bust it all up  a bodi cant tell yit which to keep way fum de water as much as you kin en dont run no resk kase it down in de bill dat yous gwyne to git hung when i lit my candl and went up to my room that night there sat pap his own self for me becaus as soon as that rise begin here come cordwood float down and piec of log raftssometim a dozen log togeth so all you have to do is to catch them and sell them to the wood yard and the ride high like a duck  i shot head first off of the bank like a frog cloth and all on and struck out for the cano  i just expect there be somebodi lay down in it becaus peopl often done that to fool folk and when a chap had pull a skiff out most to it theyd rais up and laugh at him  but it warnt so this time  it was a drift cano sure enough and i clumb in and paddl her ashor  think i the old man will be glad when he see thissh worth ten dollar  but when i got to shore pap wasnt in sight yet and as i was run her into a littl creek like a gulli all hung over with vine and willow i struck anoth idea  i judg id hide her good and then stead of take to the wood when i run off id go down the river about fifti mile and camp in one place for good and not have such a rough time tramp on foot it was pretti close to the shanti and i thought i heard the old man come all the time but i got her hid and then i out and look around a bunch of willow and there was the old man down the path a piec just draw a bead on a bird with his gun  so he hadnt seen anyth when he got along i was hard at it take up a trot line  he abus me a littl for be so slow but i told him i fell in the river and that was what made me so long  i know he would see i was wet and then he would be ask question  we got five catfish off the line and went home while we laid off after breakfast to sleep up both of us be about wore out i got to think that if i could fix up some way to keep pap and the widow from tri to follow me it would be a certain thing than trust to luck to get far enough off befor they miss me you see all kind of thing might happen  well i didnt see no way for a while but by and by pap rais up a minut to drink anoth barrel of water and he say anoth time a man come a prowl round here you roust me out you hear that man warnt here for no good  id a shot him  next time you roust me out you hear then he drop down and went to sleep again but what he had been say give me the veri idea i want  i say to myself i can fix it now so nobodi wont think of follow me about twelv oclock we turn out and went along up the bank  the river was come up pretti fast and lot of driftwood go by on the rise by and by along come part of a log raftnin log fast togeth  we went out with the skiff and tow it ashor  then we had dinner anybodi but pap would a wait and seen the day through so as to catch more stuff but that warnt pap style  nine log was enough for one time he must shove right over to town and sell  so he lock me in and took the skiff and start off tow the raft about half past three  i judg he wouldnt come back that night  i wait till i reckon he had got a good start then i out with my saw and went to work on that log again  befor he was tother side of the river i was out of the hole him and his raft was just a speck on the water away off yonder i took the sack of corn meal and took it to where the cano was hid and shove the vine and branch apart and put it in then i done the same with the side of bacon then the whiski jug  i took all the coffe and sugar there was and all the ammunit i took the wad i took the bucket and gourd i took a dipper and a tin cup and my old saw and two blanket and the skillet and the coffe pot  i took fish line and match and other thingseveryth that was worth a cent  i clean out the place  i want an axe but there wasnt ani onli the one out at the woodpil and i know whi i was go to leav that  i fetch out the gun and now i was done i had wore the ground a good deal crawl out of the hole and drag out so mani thing  so i fix that as good as i could from the outsid by scatter dust on the place which cover up the smooth and the sawdust  then i fix the piec of log back into it place and put two rock under it and one against it to hold it there for it was bent up at that place and didnt quit touch ground  if you stood four or five foot away and didnt know it was saw you wouldnt never notic it and besid this was the back of the cabin and it warnt like anybodi would go fool around there it was all grass clear to the cano so i hadnt left a track  i follow around to see  i stood on the bank and look out over the river  all safe  so i took the gun and went up a piec into the wood and was hunt around for some bird when i see a wild pig hog soon went wild in them bottom after they had got away from the prairi farm i shot this fellow and took him into camp i took the axe and smash in the door  i beat it and hack it consider a do it  i fetch the pig in and took him back near to the tabl and hack into his throat with the axe and laid him down on the ground to bleed i say ground becaus it was groundhard pack and no board  well next i took an old sack and put a lot of big rock in ital i could dragand i start it from the pig and drag it to the door and through the wood down to the river and dump it in and down it sunk out of sight  you could easi see that someth had been drag over the ground  i did wish tom sawyer was there i know he would take an interest in this kind of busi and throw in the fanci touch  nobodi could spread himself like tom sawyer in such a thing as that well last i pull out some of my hair and blood the axe good and stuck it on the back side and slung the axe in the corner  then i took up the pig and held him to my breast with my jacket so he couldnt drip till i got a good piec below the hous and then dump him into the river  now i thought of someth els  so i went and got the bag of meal and my old saw out of the cano and fetch them to the hous  i took the bag to where it use to stand and rip a hole in the bottom of it with the saw for there warnt no knive and fork on the placepap done everyth with his clasp knife about the cook  then i carri the sack about a hundr yard across the grass and through the willow east of the hous to a shallow lake that was five mile wide and full of rushesand duck too you might say in the season  there was a slough or a creek lead out of it on the other side that went mile away i dont know where but it didnt go to the river  the meal sift out and made a littl track all the way to the lake  i drop pap whetston there too so as to look like it had been done by accid then i tie up the rip in the meal sack with a string so it wouldnt leak no more and took it and my saw to the cano again it was about dark now so i drop the cano down the river under some willow that hung over the bank and wait for the moon to rise  i made fast to a willow then i took a bite to eat and by and by laid down in the cano to smoke a pipe and lay out a plan  i say to myself theyll follow the track of that sack of rock to the shore and then drag the river for me  and theyll follow that meal track to the lake and go brows down the creek that lead out of it to find the robber that kill me and took the thing  they wont ever hunt the river for anyth but my dead carcass theyll soon get tire of that and wont bother no more about me  all right i can stop anywher i want to jackson island is good enough for me i know that island pretti well and nobodi ever come there  and then i can paddl over to town night and slink around and pick up thing i want jackson island the place i was pretti tire and the first thing i know i was asleep  when i woke up i didnt know where i was for a minut  i set up and look around a littl scare  then i rememb  the river look mile and mile across  the moon was so bright i could a count the drift log that went a slip along black and still hundr of yard out from shore everyth was dead quiet and it look late and smelt late you know what i meani dont know the word to put it in i took a good gap and a stretch and was just go to unhitch and start when i heard a sound away over the water  i listen  pretti soon i made it out  it was that dull kind of a regular sound that come from oar work in rowlock when it a still night  i peep out through the willow branch and there it wasa skiff away across the water  i couldnt tell how mani was in it  it kept a come and when it was abreast of me i see there warnt but one man in it  think i mayb it pap though i warnt expect him  he drop below me with the current and by and by he came a swing up shore in the easi water and he went by so close i could a reach out the gun and touch him  well it was pap sure enoughand sober too by the way he laid his oar i didnt lose no time  the next minut i was a spin down stream soft but quick in the shade of the bank  i made two mile and a half and then struck out a quarter of a mile or more toward the middl of the river becaus pretti soon i would be pass the ferri land and peopl might see me and hail me  i got out amongst the driftwood and then laid down in the bottom of the cano and let her float  i laid there and had a good rest and a smoke out of my pipe look away into the sky not a cloud in it  the sky look ever so deep when you lay down on your back in the moonshin i never know it befor  and how far a bodi can hear on the water such night  i heard peopl talk at the ferri land i heard what they said tooeveri word of it  one man said it was get toward the long day and the short night now  tother one said this warnt one of the short one he reckonedand then they laugh and he said it over again and they laugh again then they wake up anoth fellow and told him and laugh but he didnt laugh he rip out someth brisk and said let him alon  the first fellow said he low to tell it to his old womansh would think it was pretti good but he said that warnt noth to some thing he had said in his time i heard one man say it was near three oclock and he hope daylight wouldnt wait more than about a week longer  after that the talk got further and further away and i couldnt make out the word ani more but i could hear the mumbl and now and then a laugh too but it seem a long way off i was away below the ferri now  i rose up and there was jackson island about two mile and a half down stream heavi timber and stand up out of the middl of the river big and dark and solid like a steamboat without ani light  there warnt ani sign of the bar at the headit was all under water now it didnt take me long to get there  i shot past the head at a rip rate the current was so swift and then i got into the dead water and land on the side toward the illinoi shore  i run the cano into a deep dent in the bank that i know about i had to part the willow branch to get in and when i made fast nobodi could a seen the cano from the outsid i went up and set down on a log at the head of the island and look out on the big river and the black driftwood and away over to the town three mile away where there was three or four light twinkl  a monstrous big lumber raft was about a mile up stream come along down with a lantern in the middl of it  i watch it come creep down and when it was most abreast of where i stood i heard a man say stern oar there heav her head to stabboard  i heard that just as plain as if the man was by my side there was a littl gray in the sky now so i step into the wood and laid down for a nap befor breakfast chapter viii the sun was up so high when i wake that i judg it was after eight oclock  i laid there in the grass and the cool shade think about thing and feel rest and ruther comfort and satisfi  i could see the sun out at one or two hole but most it was big tree all about and gloomi in there amongst them  there was freckl place on the ground where the light sift down through the leav and the freckl place swap about a littl show there was a littl breez up there  a coupl of squirrel set on a limb and jabber at me veri friend i was power lazi and comfortabledidnt want to get up and cook breakfast  well i was doze off again when i think i hear a deep sound of boom away up the river  i rous up and rest on my elbow and listen pretti soon i hear it again  i hop up and went and look out at a hole in the leav and i see a bunch of smoke lay on the water a long way upabout abreast the ferri  and there was the ferryboat full of peopl float along down  i know what was the matter now  boom i see the white smoke squirt out of the ferryboat side  you see they was fire cannon over the water tri to make my carcass come to the top i was pretti hungri but it warnt go to do for me to start a fire becaus they might see the smoke  so i set there and watch the cannon smoke and listen to the boom  the river was a mile wide there and it alway look pretti on a summer morningso i was have a good enough time see them hunt for my remaind if i onli had a bite to eat well then i happen to think how they alway put quicksilv in loav of bread and float them off becaus they alway go right to the drownd carcass and stop there  so say i ill keep a lookout and if ani of them float around after me ill give them a show  i chang to the illinoi edg of the island to see what luck i could have and i warnt disappoint  a big doubl loaf come along and i most got it with a long stick but my foot slip and she float out further  of cours i was where the current set in the closest to the shorei know enough for that  but by and by along come anoth one and this time i won  i took out the plug and shook out the littl dab of quicksilv and set my teeth in  it was baker breadwhat the qualiti eat none of your low down corn pone i got a good place amongst the leav and set there on a log munch the bread and watch the ferri boat and veri well satisfi  and then someth struck me  i say now i reckon the widow or the parson or somebodi pray that this bread would find me and here it has gone and done it  so there aint no doubt but there is someth in that thingthat is there someth in it when a bodi like the widow or the parson pray but it dont work for me and i reckon it dont work for onli just the right kind i lit a pipe and had a good long smoke and went on watch  the ferryboat was float with the current and i allow id have a chanc to see who was aboard when she come along becaus she would come in close where the bread did  when shed got pretti well along down toward me i put out my pipe and went to where i fish out the bread and laid down behind a log on the bank in a littl open place  where the log fork i could peep through by and by she come along and she drift in so close that they could a run out a plank and walk ashor  most everybodi was on the boat  pap and judg thatcher and bessi thatcher and jo harper and tom sawyer and his old aunt polli and sid and mari and plenti more  everybodi was talk about the murder but the captain broke in and say look sharp now the current set in the closest here and mayb hes wash ashor and got tangl amongst the brush at the water edg  i hope so anyway i didnt hope so  they all crowd up and lean over the rail near in my face and kept still watch with all their might  i could see them first rate but they couldnt see me  then the captain sung out stand away and the cannon let off such a blast right befor me that it made me deef with the nois and pretti near blind with the smoke and i judg i was gone  if theyd a had some bullet in i reckon theyd a got the corps they was after  well i see i warnt hurt thank to good the boat float on and went out of sight around the shoulder of the island  i could hear the boom now and then further and further off and by and by after an hour i didnt hear it no more  the island was three mile long  i judg they had got to the foot and was give it up  but they didnt yet a while  they turn around the foot of the island and start up the channel on the missouri side under steam and boom onc in a while as they went  i cross over to that side and watch them when they got abreast the head of the island they quit shoot and drop over to the missouri shore and went home to the town i know i was all right now  nobodi els would come a hunt after me i got my trap out of the cano and made me a nice camp in the thick wood  i made a kind of a tent out of my blanket to put my thing under so the rain couldnt get at them  i catch a catfish and haggl him open with my saw and toward sundown i start my camp fire and had supper  then i set out a line to catch some fish for breakfast when it was dark i set by my camp fire smoke and feel pretti well satisfi but by and by it got sort of lonesom and so i went and set on the bank and listen to the current swash along and count the star and drift log and raft that come down and then went to bed there aint no better way to put in time when you are lonesom you cant stay so you soon get over it and so for three day and night  no differencejust the same thing but the next day i went explor around down through the island  i was boss of it it all belong to me so to say and i want to know all about it but main i want to put in the time  i found plenti strawberri ripe and prime and green summer grape and green razberri and the green blackberri was just begin to show  they would all come handi by and by i judg well i went fool along in the deep wood till i judg i warnt far from the foot of the island  i had my gun along but i hadnt shot noth it was for protect thought i would kill some game nigh home about this time i mighti near step on a good size snake and it went slide off through the grass and flower and i after it tri to get a shot at it i clip along and all of a sudden i bound right on to the ash of a camp fire that was still smoke my heart jump up amongst my lung  i never wait for to look further but uncock my gun and went sneak back on my tipto as fast as ever i could  everi now and then i stop a second amongst the thick leav and listen but my breath come so hard i couldnt hear noth els  i slunk along anoth piec further then listen again and so on and so on  if i see a stump i took it for a man if i trod on a stick and broke it it made me feel like a person had cut one of my breath in two and i onli got half and the short half too when i got to camp i warnt feel veri brash there warnt much sand in my craw but i say this aint no time to be fool around  so i got all my trap into my cano again so as to have them out of sight and i put out the fire and scatter the ash around to look like an old last year camp and then clumb a tree i reckon i was up in the tree two hour but i didnt see noth i didnt hear nothingi onli thought i heard and seen as much as a thousand thing  well i couldnt stay up there forev so at last i got down but i kept in the thick wood and on the lookout all the time all i could get to eat was berri and what was left over from breakfast by the time it was night i was pretti hungri  so when it was good and dark i slid out from shore befor moonris and paddl over to the illinoi bankabout a quarter of a mile  i went out in the wood and cook a supper and i had about made up my mind i would stay there all slow  bi and by i was close enough to have a look and there laid a man on the ground  it most give me the fan tod he had a blanket around his head and his head was near in the fire  i set there behind the ten dollar no i didnt lose it all  i oni los bout nine of it  i sole de hide en taller for a dollar en ten cent you had five dollar and ten cent left  did you specul ani more yes  you know that one laig nigger dat blong to old misto bradish well he sot up a bank en say anybodi dat put in a dollar would git fo dollar mo at de en er de year  well all de nigger went in but dey didnt have much your go to be rich again some time or other yes en is rich now come to look at it  i own mysef en is wuth eight hundd dollar  i wisht i had de money i wouldn want no mo chapter ix i want to go and look at a place right about the middl of the island that id found when i was explor so we start and soon got to it becaus the island was onli three mile long and a quarter of a mile wide this place was a toler long steep hill or ridg about forti foot high we had a rough time get to the top the side was so steep and the bush so thick  we tramp and clumb around all over it and by and by found a good big cavern in the rock most up to the top on the side toward illinoi  the cavern was as big as two or three room bunch togeth and jim could stand up straight in it  it was cool in there jim was for put our trap in there right away but i said we didnt want to be climb up and down there all the time jim said if we had the cano hid in a good place and had all the trap in the cavern we could rush there if anybodi was to come to the island and they would never find us without dog  and besid he said them littl bird had said it was go to rain and did i want the thing to get wet so we went back and got the cano and paddl up abreast the cavern and lug all the trap up there  then we hunt up a place close by to hide the cano in amongst the thick willow  we took some fish off of the line and set them again and begun to get readi for dinner the door of the cavern was big enough to roll a hogshead in and on one side of the door the floor stuck out a littl bit and was flat and a good place to build a fire on  so we built it there and cook dinner we spread the blanket insid for a carpet and eat our dinner in there we put all the other thing handi at the back of the cavern  pretti soon it darken up and begun to thunder and lighten so the bird was right about it  direct it begun to rain and it rain like all furi too and i never see the wind blow so  it was one of these regular summer storm  it would get so dark that it look all blue black outsid and love and the rain would thrash along by so thick that the tree off a littl way look dim and spider webbi and here would come a blast of wind that would bend the tree down and turn up the pale undersid of the leav and then a perfect ripper of a gust would follow along and set the branch to toss their arm as if they was just wild and next when it was just about the bluest and blackest fst it was as bright as glori and youd have a littl glimps of tree top a plung about away off yonder in the storm hundr of yard further chile the river went on rais and rais for ten or twelv day till at last it was over the bank  the water was three or four foot deep on the island in the low place and on the illinoi bottom  on that other way  well on everi old broken down tree you could see rabbit and snake and such thing and when the island had been overflow a day or two they got so tame on account of be hungri that you could a big bend on the illinoi side and hack off cottonwood branch with the hatchet and cover up the raft with them so she look like there had been a cave in in the bank there  a tow head is a sandbar that has cottonwood on it as thick as harrow teeth we had mountain on the missouri shore and heavi timber on the illinoi side and the channel was down the missouri shore at that place so we warnt afraid of anybodi run across us  we laid there all day and watch the raft and steamboat spin down the missouri shore and up bound steamboat fight the big river in the middl  i told jim all about the time i had jabber with that woman and jim said she was a smart one and if she was to start after us herself she wouldnt set down and watch a camp fireno sir shed fetch a dog  well then i said whi couldnt she tell her husband to fetch a dog  jim said he bet she did think of it by the time the men was readi to start and he believ they must a gone up town to get a dog and so they lost all that time or els we wouldnt be here on a towhead sixteen or seventeen mile below the villageno indeedi we would be in that same old town again  so i said i didnt care what was the reason they didnt get us as long as they didnt when it was begin to come on dark we poke our head out of the cottonwood thicket and look up and down and across noth in sight so jim took up some of the top plank of the raft and built a snug wigwam to get under in blaze weather and raini and to keep the thing dri jim made a floor for the wigwam and rais it a foot or more abov the level of the raft so now the blanket and all the trap was out of reach of steamboat wave  right in the middl of the wigwam we made a layer of dirt about five or six inch deep with a frame around it for to hold it to it place this was to build a fire on in sloppi weather or chilli the wigwam would keep it from be seen  we made an extra steer oar too becaus one of the other might get broke on a snag or someth we fix up a short fork stick to hang the old lantern on becaus we must alway light the lantern whenev we see a steamboat come down stream to keep from get run over but we wouldnt have to light it for up stream boat unless we see we was in what they call a cross for the river was pretti high yet veri low bank be still a littl under water so up bound boat didnt alway run the channel but hunt easi water this second night we run between seven and eight hour with a current that was make over four mile an hour  we catch fish and talk and we took a swim now and then to keep off sleepi  it was kind of solemn drift down the big still river lay on our back look up at the star and we didnt ever feel like talk loud and it warnt often that we laughedon a littl kind of a low chuckl  we had mighti good weather as a general thing and noth ever happen to us at allthat night nor the next nor the next everi night we pass town some of them away up on black hillsid noth but just a shini bed of light not a hous could you see  the fifth night we pass st loui and it was like the whole world lit up in st petersburg they use to say there was twenti or thirti thousand peopl in st loui but i never believ it till i see that wonder spread of light at two oclock that still night  there warnt a sound there everybodi was asleep everi night now i use to slip ashor toward ten oclock at some littl villag and buy ten or fifteen cent worth of meal or bacon or other stuff to eat and sometim i lift a chicken that warnt roost comfort and took him along  pap alway said take a chicken when you get a chanc becaus if you dont want him yourself you can easi find somebodi that doe and a good deed aint ever forgot  i never see pap when he didnt want the chicken himself but that is what he use to say anyway morn befor daylight i slip into cornfield and warnt anyth but a soft name for steal and no decent bodi would do it  jim said he reckon the widow was part right and pap was part right so the best way would be for us to pick out two or three thing from the list and say we wouldnt borrow them ani morethen he reckon it wouldnt be no harm to borrow the other  so we talk it over all one night drift along down the river tri to make up our mind whether to drop the watermelon or the cantelop or the mushmelon or what  but toward daylight we got it all settl satisfactori and conclud to drop crabappl and psimmon  we warnt feel just right befor that but it was all comfort now  i was glad the way it come out too becaus crabappl aint ever good and the psimmon wouldnt be ripe for two or three month yet we shot a water fowl now and then that got up too earli in the morn or didnt go to bed earli enough in the even  take it all round we live pretti high the fifth night below st loui we had a big storm after midnight with a power of thunder and lightn and the rain pour down in a solid sheet we stay in the wigwam and let the raft take care of itself when the lightn glare out we could see a big straight river ahead and high rocki bluff on both all right as far as it went but the towhead warnt sixti yard long and the minut i flew by the foot of it i shot out into the solid white fog and hadnt no more idea which way i was go than a dead man think i it wont do to paddl first i know ill run into the bank or a towhead or someth i got to set still and float and yet it mighti fidgeti busi to have to hold your hand still at such a time  i whoop and listen  away down there somewher i hear a small whoop and up come my spirit  i went tear after it listen sharp to hear it again  the next time it come i see i warnt head for it but head away to the right of it  and the next time i was head away to the left of itand not gain on it much either for i was fli around this way and that and tother but it was go straight ahead all the time i did wish the fool would think to beat a tin pan and beat it all the time but he never did and it was the still place between the whoop that was make the troubl for me  well i fought along and direct i hear the whoop behind me  i was tangl good now  that was somebodi els whoop or els i was turn around i throw the paddl down  i heard the whoop again it was behind me yet but in a differ place it kept come and kept chang it place and i kept answer till by and by it was in front of me again and i know the current had swung the cano head down stream and i was all right if that was jim and not some other raftsman holler  i couldnt tell noth about voic in a fog for noth dont look natur nor sound natur in a fog the whoop went on and in about a minut i come a boom down on a cut bank with smoki ghost of big tree on it and the current throw me off to the left and shot by amongst a lot of snag that fair roar the currrent was tear by them so swift in anoth second or two it was solid white and still again  i set perfect still then listen to my heart thump and i reckon i didnt draw a breath while it thump a hundr i just give up then  i know what the matter was  that cut bank was an island and jim had gone down tother side of it  it warnt no towhead that you could float by in ten minut  it had the big timber of a regular island it might be five or six mile long and more than half a mile wide i kept quiet with my ear cock about fifteen minut i reckon  i was float along of cours four or five mile an hour but you dont ever think of that  no you feel like you are lay dead still on the water and if a littl glimps of a snag slip by you dont think to yourself how fast your go but you catch your breath and think my how that snag tear along  if you think it aint dismal and lonesom out in a fog that way by yourself in the night you tri it onceyoul see next for about a half an hour i whoop now and then at last i hear the answer a long way off and tri to follow it but i couldnt do it and direct i judg id got into a nest of towhead for i had littl dim glimps of them on both side of mesometim just a narrow channel between and some that i couldnt see i know was there becaus id hear the wash of the current against the old dead brush and trash that hung over the bank  well i warnt long loos the whoop down amongst the towhead and i onli tri to chase them a littl while anyway becaus it was wors than chase a jack o lantern  you never know a sound dodg around so and swap place so quick and so much i had to claw away from the bank pretti live four or five time to keep from knock the island out of the river and so i judg the raft must be but into the bank everi now and then or els it would get further ahead and clear out of hearingit was float a littl faster than what i was well i the cano and said i wouldnt bother no more  i didnt want to go to sleep of cours but i was so sleepi i couldnt help it so i thought i would take jest one littl cat nap but i reckon it was more than a back to me they seem to come up dim out of last week it was a monstrous big river here with the tallest and the thickest kind of timber on both bank just a solid wall as well as i could see by the never heard tell of it befor but you can guess cant you  it just as easi which candl  i say whi ani candl he say i dont know where he was say i where was he whi he was in the dark  that where he was confound these ole britch  i reckon id better put em on but id ruther not it so warm  are you all readi all right  come along old hoss cold corn pone cold corn beef butter and buttermilkthat is what they had for me down there and there aint noth better that ever ive come across yet  buck and his ma and all of them smoke cob pipe except the nigger woman which was gone and the two young women  they all smoke and talk and i eat and talk  the young women had quilt around them and their hair down their back  they all ask me question and i told them how pap and me and all the famili was live on a littl farm down at the bottom of arkansaw and my sister mari ann run off and got marri and never was heard of no more and bill went to hunt them and he warnt heard of no more and tom and mort die and then there warnt nobodi but just me and pap left and he was just trim down to noth on account of his troubl so when he die i took what there was left becaus the farm didnt belong to us and start up the river deck passag and fell overboard and that was how i come to be here  so they said i could have a home there as long as i want it  then it was most daylight and everybodi went to bed and i went to bed with buck and when i wake up in the morn drat it all i had forgot what my name was so i laid there about an hour tri to think and when buck wake up i say can you spell buck yes he say i bet you cant spell my name say i i bet you what you dare i can say he all right say i go ahead g e o r g e j a x o nthere now he say well say i you done it but i didnt think you could  it aint no slouch of a name to spellright off without studi i set it down privat becaus somebodi might want me to spell it next and so i want to be handi with it and rattl it off like i was use to it it was a mighti nice famili and a mighti nice hous too  i hadnt seen no hous out in the countri befor that was so nice and had so much style  it didnt have an iron latch on the front door nor a wooden one with a buckskin string but a brass knob to turn the same as hous in town there warnt no bed in the parlor nor a sign of a bed but heap of parlor in town has bed in them  there was a big fireplac that was brick on the bottom and the brick was kept clean and red by pour water on them and scrub them with anoth brick sometim they wash them over with red water paint that they call spanish brown same as they do in town  they had big brass dog iron that could hold up a saw log there was a clock on the middl of the mantelpiec with a pictur of a town paint on the bottom half of the glass front and a round place in the middl of it for the sun and you could see the pendulum swing behind it  it was beauti to hear that clock tick and sometim when one of these peddler had been along and scour her up and got her in good shape she would start in and strike a hundr and fifti befor she got tucker out  they wouldnt took ani money for her well there was a big outlandish parrot on each side of the clock made out of someth like chalk and paint up gaudi  bi one of the parrot was a cat made of crockeri and a crockeri dog by the other and when you press down on them they squeak but didnt open their mouth nor look differ nor interest  they squeak through underneath  there was a coupl of big wild turkey wing fan spread out behind those thing  on the tabl in the middl of the room was a kind of a love crockeri basket that had appl and orang and peach and grape pile up in it which was much redder and yellow and prettier than real one is but they warnt real becaus you could see where piec had got chip off and show the white chalk or whatev it was underneath this tabl had a cover made out of beauti oilcloth with a red and blue spread eagl paint on it and a paint border all around  it come all the way from philadelphia they said  there was some book too pile up perfect exact on each corner of the tabl  one was a big famili bibl full of pictur  one was pilgrim progress about a man that left his famili it didnt say whi  i read consider in it now and then  the statement was interest but tough  anoth was friendship offer full of beauti stuff and poetri but i didnt read the poetri  anoth was henri clay speech and anoth was dr gunn famili medicin which told you all about what to do if a bodi was sick or dead  there was a hymn book and a lot of other book  and there was nice split bottom chair and perfect sound toonot bag down in the middl and bust like an old basket they had pictur hung on the wallsmain washington and lafayett and battl and highland mari and one call sign the declar there was some that they call crayon which one of the daughter which was dead made her own self when she was onli fifteen year old  they was differ from ani pictur i ever see beforeblack most than is common  one was a woman in a slim black dress belt small under the armpit with bulg like a cabbag in the middl of the sleev and a larg black scoop shovel bonnet with a black veil and white slim ankl cross front of a comb like a chair back and she was cri into a handkerchief and had a dead bird lay on it back in her other hand with it heel up and underneath the pictur it said i shall never hear thi sweet chirrup more ala  there was one where a young ladi was at a window look up at the moon and tear run down her cheek and she had an open letter in one hand with black seal wax show on one edg of it and she was mash a locket with a chain to it against her mouth and underneath the pictur it said and art thou gone yes thou art gone ala  these was all nice pictur i reckon but i didnt somehow seem to take to them becaus if ever i was down a littl they alway give me the fan tod  everybodi was sorri she die becaus she had laid out a lot more of these pictur to do and a bodi could see by what she had done what they had lost  but i reckon that with her disposit she was have a better time in the graveyard  she was at work on what they said was her greatest pictur when she took sick and everi day and everi night it was her prayer to be allow to live till she got it done but she never got the chanc  it was a pictur of a young woman in a long white gown stand on the rail of a bridg all readi to jump off with her hair all down her back and look up to the moon with the tear run down her face and she had two arm fold across her breast and two arm stretch out in front and two more reach up toward the moonand the idea was to see which pair would look best and then scratch out all the other arm but as i was say she die befor she got her mind made up and now they kept this pictur over the head of the bed in her room and everi time her birthday come they hung flower on it  other time it was hid with a littl curtain  the young woman in the pictur had a kind of a nice sweet face but there was so mani arm it made her look too spideri seem to me this young girl kept a scrap book when she was aliv and use to past obituari and accid and case of patient suffer in it out of the presbyterian observ and write poetri after them out of her own head it was veri good poetri this is what she wrote about a boy by the name of stephen dowl bot that fell down a well and was drownd ode to stephen on it  the wall of all the room was plaster and most had carpet on the floor and the whole hous was whitewash on the outsid it was a doubl hous and the big open place betwixt them was roof and floor and sometim the tabl was set there in the middl of the day and it was a cool comfort place  noth couldnt be better  and warnt the cook good and just bushel of it too chapter xviii col  grangerford was a gentleman you see  he was a gentleman all over and so was his famili  he was well born as the say is and that worth as much in a man as it is in a hors so the widow dougla said and nobodi ever deni that she was of the first aristocraci in our town and pap he alway said it too though he warnt no more qualiti than a mudcat himself  col  grangerford was veri tall and veri slim and had a darkish pali complexion not a sign of red in it anywher he was clean shave everi morn all over his thin face and he had the thinnest kind of lip and the thinnest kind of nostril and a high nose and heavi eyebrow and the blackest kind of eye sunk so deep back that they seem like they was look out of cavern at you as you may say  his forehead was high and his hair was black and straight and hung to his shoulder his hand was long and thin and everi day of his life he put on a clean shirt and a full suit from head to foot made out of linen so white it hurt your eye to look at it and on sunday he wore a blue tail coat with brass button on it  he carri a mahogani cane with a silver head to it  there warnt no frivolish about him not a bit and he warnt ever loud  he was as kind as he could beyou could feel that you know and so you had confid  sometim he smile and it was good to see but when he straighten himself up like a liberti pole and the lightn begun to flicker out from under his eyebrow you want to climb a tree first and find out what the matter was afterward  he didnt ever have to tell anybodi to mind their mannerseverybodi was alway good manner where he was  everybodi love to have him around too he was sunshin most alwaysi mean he made it seem like good weather  when he turn into a cloudbank it was aw dark for half a minut and that was enough there wouldnt noth go wrong again for a week when him and the old ladi come down in the morn all the famili got up out of their chair and give them good day and didnt set down again till they had set down  then tom and bob went to the sideboard where the decant was and mix a glass of bitter and hand it to him and he held it in his hand and wait till tom and bob was mix and then they bow and said our duti to you sir and madam and they bow the least bit in the world and said thank you and so they drank all three and bob and tom pour a spoon of water on the sugar and the mite of whiski or appl brandi in the bottom of their tumbler and give it to me and buck and we drank to the old peopl too bob was the oldest and tom nexttal beauti men with veri broad shoulder and brown face and long black hair and black eye  they dress in white linen from head to foot like the old gentleman and wore broad panama hat then there was miss charlott she was twenti five and tall and proud and grand but as good as she could be when she warnt stir up but when she was she had a look that would make you wilt in your track like her father  she was beauti so was her sister miss sophia but it was a differ kind  she was gentl and sweet like a dove and she was onli twenti each person had their own nigger to wait on thembuck too  mi nigger had a monstrous easi time becaus i warnt use to have anybodi do anyth for me but buck was on the jump most of the time this was all there was of the famili now but there use to be morethre son they got kill and emmelin that die the old gentleman own a lot of farm and over a hundr nigger sometim a stack of peopl would come there horseback from ten or fifteen mile around and stay five or six day and have such junket round about and on the river and danc and picnic in the wood daytim and ball at the hous night  these peopl was most kinfolk of the famili  the men brought their gun with them  it was a handsom lot of qualiti i tell you there was anoth clan of aristocraci around theref or six familiesmost of the name of shepherdson  they was as high tone and well born and rich and grand as the tribe of grangerford  the shepherdson and grangerford use the same steamboat land which was about two mile abov our hous so sometim when i went up there with a lot of our folk i use to see a lot of the shepherdson there on their fine hors one day buck and me was away out in the wood hunt and heard a hors come  we was cross the road  buck say quick  jump for the wood we done it and then peep down the wood through the leav  pretti soon a splendid young man come gallop down the road set his hors easi and look like a soldier  he had his gun across his pommel  i had seen him befor  it was young harney shepherdson  i heard buck gun go off at my ear and harney hat tumbl off from his head  he grab his gun and rode straight to the place where we was hid  but we didnt wait  we start through the wood on a run  the wood warnt thick so i look over my shoulder to dodg the bullet and twice i seen harney cover buck with his gun and then he rode away the way he cometo get his hat i reckon but i couldnt see  we never stop run till we got home  the old gentleman eye blaze a minutetwa pleasur main i judgedthen his face sort of smooth down and he say kind of gentl i dont like that shoot from behind a bush  whi didnt you step into the road my boy the shepherdson dont father  they alway take advantag miss charlott she held her head up like a queen while buck was tell his tale and her nostril spread and her eye snap  the two young men look dark but never said noth  miss sophia she turn pale but the color come back when she found the man warnt hurt soon as i could get buck down by the corn crib under the tree by ourselv i say did you want to kill him buck well i bet i did what did he do to you him  he never done noth to me well then what did you want to kill him for whi nothingon it on account of the feud what a feud whi where was you rais  dont you know what a feud is never heard of it beforetel me about it well say buck a feud is this way  a man has a quarrel with anoth man and kill him then that other man brother kill him then the other brother on both side goe for one anoth then the cousin chip inand by and by everybodi kill off and there aint no more feud  but it kind of slow and take a long time has this one been go on long buck well i should reckon  it start thirti year ago or somer along there  there was troubl bout someth and then a lawsuit to settl it and the suit went agin one of the men and so he up and shot the man that won the suitwhich he would natur do of cours  anybodi would what was the troubl about buckland i reckon maybei dont know well who done the shoot  was it a grangerford or a shepherdson law how do i know  it was so long ago dont anybodi know oh yes pa know i reckon and some of the other old peopl but they dont know now what the row was about in the first place has there been mani kill buck yes right smart chanc of funer  but they dont alway kill  pas got a few buckshot in him but he dont mind it cuz he dont weigh much anyway  bob been carv up some with a bowi and tom been hurt onc or twice has anybodi been kill this year buck yes we got one and they got one  bout three month ago my cousin bud fourteen year old was ride through the wood on tother side of the river and didnt have no weapon with him which was blame foolish and in a lonesom place he hear a hors a come behind him and see old baldi shepherdson a linkin after him with his gun in his hand and his white hair a fli in the wind and stead of jump off and take to the brush bud low he could out run him so they had it nip and tuck for five mile or more the old man a gain all the time so at last bud seen it warnt ani use so he stop and face around so as to have the bullet hole in front you know and the old man he rode up and shot him down  but he didnt git much chanc to enjoy his luck for insid of a week our folk laid him out i reckon that old man was a coward buck i reckon he warnt a coward  not by a blame sight  there aint a coward amongst them shepherdsonsnot a one  and there aint no coward amongst the grangerford either  whi that old man kep up his end in a fight one day for half an hour against three grangerford and come out winner  they was all a horseback he lit off of his hors and got behind a littl woodpil and kep his hors befor him to stop the bullet but the grangerford stay on their hors and caper around the old man and pepper away at him and he pepper away at them  him and his hors both went home pretti leaki and crippl but the grangerford had to be fetch homeand one of em was dead and anoth die the next day  no sir if a bodi out hunt for coward he dont want to fool away ani time amongst them shepherdson becuz they dont breed ani of that kind next sunday we all went to church about three mile everybodi a horseback the men took their gun along so did buck and kept them between their knee or stood them handi against the wall  the shepherdson done the same  it was pretti orneri preachingal about brother love and such like tiresom but everybodi said it was a good sermon and they all talk it over go home and had after dinner everybodi was doze around some in their chair and some in their room and it got to be pretti dull  buck and a dog was stretch out on the grass in the sun sound asleep  i went up to our room and judg i would take a nap myself  i found that sweet miss sophia stand in her door which was next to our and she took me in her room and shut the door veri soft and ask me if i like her and i said i did and she ask me if i would do someth for her and not tell anybodi and i said i would  then she said shed forgot her testament and left it in the seat at church between two other book and would i slip out quiet and go there and fetch it to her and not say noth to nobodi  i said i would so i slid out and slip off up the road and there warnt anybodi at the church except mayb a hog or two for there warnt ani lock on the door and hog like a puncheon floor in summer time becaus it cool  if you notic most folk dont go to church onli when theyv got to but a hog is differ say i to myself someth up it aint natur for a girl to be in such a sweat about a testament  so i give it a shake and out drop a littl piec of paper with half past two wrote on it with a pencil  i ransack it but couldnt find anyth els  i couldnt make anyth out of that so i put the paper in the book again and when i got home and upstair there was miss sophia in her door wait for me  she pull me in and shut the door then she look in the testament till she found the paper and as soon as she read it she look glad and befor a bodi could think she grab me and give me a squeez and said i was the best boy in the world and not to tell anybodi  she was mighti red in the face for a minut and her eye light up and it made her power pretti  i was a good deal astonish but when i got my breath i ask her what the paper was about and she ask me if i had read it and i said no and she ask me if i could read write and i told her no onli coars hand and then she said the paper warnt anyth but a book mark to keep her place and i might go and play now i went off down to the river studi over this thing and pretti soon i notic that my nigger was follow along behind  when we was out of sight of the hous he look back and around a second and then come a run and say mar jawg if youll come down into de swamp ill show you a whole stack o water moccasin think i that mighti curious he said that yesterday  he oughter
